62233291159769128>7/14/2024 11:24 PM</a></span></div><div class="chatlog__content chatlog__markdown"><span class=chatlog__markdown-preserve>I think with all things, it&#39;s just trade offs. <div class=chatlog__message-group><div id=chatlog__message-container-1263402504813805580 class=chatlog__message-container data-message-id=1263402504813805580><div class=chatlog__message><div class=chatlog__message-aside><img class=chatlog__avatar src=https://cdn.discordapp.com/embed/avatars/2.png alt=Avatar loading=lazy></div><div class=chatlog__message-primary><div class=chatlog__header><span class=chatlog__author title=neutralmilfhotel9728 data-user-id=984277984829636618>NeutralMilfHotel</span> <span class=chatlog__timestamp title="Thursday, July 18, 2024 4:50 AM"><a href=#chatlog__message-container-1263402504813805580>7/18/2024 4:50 AM</a></span></div><div class="chatlog__content chatlog__markdown"><span class=chatlog__markdown-preserve>TL;DR client wants the code for extraction and sending data to run on <em>their</em> server and not expose an API or something (and instead send it to our endpoint)...so, current rudimentary solution is:

Fetch(timerange)
  data = get_data(timerange)
  task = Post.delay(data, timerange)
  return {task.id, status}

Post(data, timerange)
  POST(endpoint, data)
  return {success message}

Both Fetch and Post are celery tasks.

1) I&#39;m unsure if the above means all the queried data (which can be a lot) is dumped into the message queue and if it can handle that
2) if this is a necessary way of doing things at all. The idea is that failures etc would simply rerun the currently polled task</span> <span class=chatlog__edited-timestamp title="Thursday, July 18, 2024 4:53 AM">(edited)</span></div></div></div></div></div>

<div class=chatlog__message-group><div id=chatlog__message-container-1263447955248119889 class=chatlog__message-container data-message-id=1263447955248119889><div class=chatlog__message><div class=chatlog__message-aside><img class=chatlog__avatar src=https://cdn.discordapp.com/embed/avatars/2.png alt=Avatar loading=lazy></div><div class=chatlog__message-primary><div class=chatlog__header><span class=chatlog__author title=neutralmilfhotel9728 data-user-id=984277984829636618>NeutralMilfHotel</span> <span class=chatlog__timestamp title="Thursday, July 18, 2024 7:51 AM"><a href=#chatlog__message-container-1263447955248119889>7/18/2024 7:51 AM</a></span></div><div class="chatlog__content chatlog__markdown"><span class=chatlog__markdown-preserve>I think celery is essentially being used as a scheduled here. Generating a beat every 30 minutes to raise a request to fetch data and post it.

The reason data is being run over an API call is because
1) the client has refused to provide any inbound access of any sort. They want this code to run on their server and send files over to us.
2) the API it&#39;s sending data over to is ours, where we&#39;ll process and store into S3.
3) because of concerns with moving around of moving around filesystems (re: could be azure instead of S3 tomorrow) and the client having delays in any code change that we&#39;d propagate to them, it was decided it&#39;s maybe best just to send to the API which we can then control.

I know that using a message queue as essentially a temp data store is not ideal, nor is sending very large swathes of data over a POST request, but this is the current state for this particular client.

I would honestly just want to remove everything and make a simple batch job that directly dumps data into our bucket, and for that I&#39;m looking to see if the current approach is enough of an operational pain / has significant bottlenecks to justify ripping it off.

Thanks in advance </span></div></div><div class=chatlog__header><span class=chatlog__author title=wh00h00 data-user-id=689583717064114274>Wh00h00</span> <span class=chatlog__timestamp title="Friday, July 19, 2024 1:26 PM"><a href=#chatlog__message-container-1263894717683466313>7/19/2024 1:26 PM</a></span></div><div class="chatlog__content chatlog__markdown"><span class=chatlog__markdown-preserve>Re-reading your post, are you talking more about stuff like DRY, clean code principles, extendable and maintainable code bases? 

You can&#39;t unless people actually care about issues. Most people don&#39;t prioritize data testing until a  major bad experience cause it&#39;s too costly or not enough capacity. 

That being said, you can start with data tests ( mainly expected values, relationships tests and baseline not null , uniqueness tests), and then build from there. On the actual pipeline front.. 

There&#39;s a reason ELT is more liked than ETL, you just bring in whatever at the speed of business , and deal with it later, and that&#39;s usually done with schema checks, checksum tables etc.</span></div></div></div></div></div>

# Initialize SparkSession with S3 configurations
spark = SparkSession.builder \
    .appName(&quot;S3 Write Example&quot;) \
    .config(&quot;spark.hadoop.fs.s3a.access.key&quot;, &quot;[redacted]&quot;) \
    .config(&quot;spark.hadoop.fs.s3a.secret.key&quot;, &quot;[redacted]&quot;) \
    .config(&quot;spark.hadoop.fs.s3a.endpoint&quot;, &quot;s3.us-east-2.amazonaws.com&quot;) \

    .config(&quot;spark.hadoop.fs.s3a.connection.timeout&quot;, &quot;5000&quot;) \
    .config(&quot;spark.hadoop.fs.s3a.socket.timeout&quot;, &quot;5000&quot;) \
    .config(&quot;spark.hadoop.fs.s3a.impl&quot;, &quot;org.apache.hadoop.fs.s3a.S3AFileSystem&quot;) \
    .getOrCreate()

# Create a simple DataFrame
data = [(&quot;John&quot;, &quot;Doe&quot;, 30), (&quot;Jane&quot;, &quot;Doe&quot;, 25)]
columns = [&quot;first_name&quot;, &quot;last_name&quot;, &quot;age&quot;]

df = spark.createDataFrame(data, columns)

# S3 bucket path
s3_bucket_path = &quot;s3a://sayeds-aws-bucket/data-folder/data.parquet&quot;

try:
    # Write the DataFrame to S3 in Parquet format
    df.write.mode(&quot;overwrite&quot;).parquet(s3_bucket_path)
    print(f&#39;Successfully uploaded DataFrame to s3://sayeds-aws-bucket/data-folder/data.parquet&#39;)
except Exception as e:
    print(f&#39;An error occurred: {e}&#39;)

# Stop the Spark session
spark.stop()</code></span> <span class=chatlog__edited-timestamp title="Friday, July 19, 2024 5:50 PM">(edited)</span></div></div></div></div></div>

import os 

# Initialize SparkSession with S3 configurations

spark = SparkSession.builder \
    .appName(&quot;S3 Write Example&quot;) \
    .config(&quot;spark.hadoop.fs.s3a.access.key&quot;, os.getenv(&quot;ACCESS_KEY&quot;)) \
    .config(&quot;spark.hadoop.fs.s3a.secret.key&quot;, os.getenv(&quot;SECRET_KEY&quot;)) \
    .config(&quot;spark.hadoop.fs.s3a.endpoint&quot;, &quot;s3.us-east-2.amazonaws.com&quot;) \

    .config(&quot;spark.hadoop.fs.s3a.connection.timeout&quot;, &quot;5000&quot;) \
    .config(&quot;spark.hadoop.fs.s3a.socket.timeout&quot;, &quot;5000&quot;) \
    .config(&quot;spark.hadoop.fs.s3a.impl&quot;, &quot;org.apache.hadoop.fs.s3a.S3AFileSystem&quot;) \
    .getOrCreate()

data = [(&quot;John&quot;, &quot;Doe&quot;, 30), (&quot;Jane&quot;, &quot;Doe&quot;, 25)]
columns = [&quot;first_name&quot;, &quot;last_name&quot;, &quot;age&quot;]

# S3 bucket path
s3_bucket_path = &quot;s3a://sayeds-aws-bucket/data-folder/data.parquet&quot;


df.write.mode(&quot;overwrite&quot;).parquet(s3_bucket_path)

spark.stop()</code></span></div></div></div></div></div>

def init_spark() -&gt; SparkSession:
    config = (
        SparkSession.builder()
        .config(
            &quot;spark.jars.packages&quot;,
            &quot;org.apache.hadoop:hadoop-aws:3.3.4,&quot;
            &quot;com.amazonaws:aws-java-sdk-core:1.12.725,&quot;
            &quot;com.amazonaws:aws-java-sdk-dynamodb:1.12.725,&quot;
            &quot;com.amazonaws:aws-java-sdk-s3:1.12.725,&quot;
            &quot;com.amazonaws:aws-java-sdk:1.12.725&quot;,
        )
        .config(&quot;spark.hadoop.fs.s3a.access.key&quot;, os.getenv(&quot;AWS_ACCESS_KEY_ID&quot;))
        .config(&quot;spark.hadoop.fs.s3a.secret.key&quot;, os.getenv(&quot;AWS_SECRET_ACCESS_KEY&quot;))
        .config(
            &quot;fs.s3a.aws.credentials.provider&quot;,
            &quot;org.apache.hadoop.fs.s3a.AnonymousAWSCredentialsProvider&quot;,
        )
        .config(&quot;spark.executor.memory&quot;, &quot;8g&quot;)
        .config(&quot;spark.driver.memory&quot;, &quot;8g&quot;)
        .getOrCreate()
    )


spark = SparkSession.builder.getOrCreate()
# Create a simple DataFrame
data = [(&quot;John&quot;, &quot;Doe&quot;, 30), (&quot;Jane&quot;, &quot;Doe&quot;, 25)]
columns = [&quot;first_name&quot;, &quot;last_name&quot;, &quot;age&quot;]

df = spark.createDataFrame(data, columns)

# S3 bucket path
s3_bucket_path = &quot;s3a://sayeds-aws-bucket/data-folder/data.parquet&quot;


df.write.mode(&quot;overwrite&quot;).parquet(s3_bucket_path)

spark.stop()</code></span></div></div></div></div><div id=chatlog__message-container-1264223792910172241 class=chatlog__message-container data-message-id=1264223792910172241><div class=chatlog__message><div class=chatlog__message-aside><div class=chatlog__short-timestamp title="Saturday, July 20, 2024 11:14 AM">11:14 AM</div></div><div class=chatlog__message-primary><div class="chatlog__content chatlog__markdown"><span class=chatlog__markdown-preserve>Something like this I assume?</span></div></div></div></div><div id=chatlog__message-container-1264223858060300399 class=chatlog__message-container data-message-id=1264223858060300399><div class=chatlog__message><div class=chatlog__message-aside><div class=chatlog__short-timestamp title="Saturday, July 20, 2024 11:14 AM">11:14 AM</div></div><div class=chatlog__message-primary><div class="chatlog__content chatlog__markdown"><span class=chatlog__markdown-preserve>Still gave the same error, but I&#39;m not sure if I configured it right</span></div></div></div></div><div id=chatlog__message-container-1264224002658926603 class=chatlog__message-container data-message-id=1264224002658926603><div class=chatlog__message><div class=chatlog__message-aside><div class=chatlog__short-timestamp title="Saturday, July 20, 2024 11:14 AM">11:14 AM</div></div><div class=chatlog__message-primary><div class="chatlog__content chatlog__markdown"><span class=chatlog__markdown-preserve>Maybe I need to have all those packages installed in the cluster</span></div></div></div></div></div>

<ul><li>Perform each analysis independently, and then (left) join it back on to the original dataset after each step so you aren&#39;t working with n^2 data at each stage</li><li>If it suits your requirements, filter the dataset after each analysis to reduce the quadratic duplication</li><li>If you&#39;re comparing every item to every other item, see if you can also add <code class="chatlog__markdown-pre chatlog__markdown-pre--inline">WHERE left.hotelCode &lt; right.hotelCode</code> or similar so you don&#39;t end up with two rows for each comparison (assuming the comparison is commutative)</li></ul></span> <span class=chatlog__edited-timestamp title="Thursday, July 25, 2024 8:27 AM">(edited)</span></div></div></div></div></div>

<div class=chatlog__message-group><div id=chatlog__message-container-1266046897131618345 class=chatlog__message-container data-message-id=1266046897131618345><div class=chatlog__message><div class=chatlog__message-aside><div class=chatlog__reply-symbol></div><img class=chatlog__avatar src="https://cdn.discordapp.com/avatars/690238531557261314/9188e5de8b4c09b67c839aa3db43379f.png?size=512" alt=Avatar loading=lazy></div><div class=chatlog__message-primary><div class=chatlog__reply><img class=chatlog__reply-avatar src="https://cdn.discordapp.com/avatars/105378403699408896/6ad9a21f4adaeee654f83a08a1327a68.png?size=512" alt=Avatar loading=lazy><div class=chatlog__reply-author style=color:rgb(231,76,60) title=emikachi>emily</div><div class=chatlog__reply-content><span class=chatlog__reply-link onclick="scrollToMessage(event,'1265993441096110120')"> A few things:
<ul><li>Perform each analysis independently, and then (left) join it back on to the original dataset after each step so you aren&#39;t working with n^2 data at each stage</li><li>If it suits your requirements, filter the dataset after each analysis to reduce the quadratic duplication</li><li>If you&#39;re comparing every item to every other item, see if you can also add <code class="chatlog__markdown-pre chatlog__markdown-pre--inline">WHERE left.hotelCode &lt; right.hotelCode</code> or similar so you don&#39;t end up with two rows for each comparison (assuming the comparison is commutative)</li></ul> </span> <span class=chatlog__reply-edited-timestamp title="Thursday, July 25, 2024 8:27 AM">(edited)</span></div></div><div class=chatlog__header><span class=chatlog__author style=color:rgb(52,152,219) title=abd7730 data-user-id=690238531557261314>abd</span> <span class=chatlog__timestamp title="Thursday, July 25, 2024 11:58 AM"><a href=#chatlog__message-container-1266046897131618345>7/25/2024 11:58 AM</a></span></div><div class="chatlog__content chatlog__markdown"><span class=chatlog__markdown-preserve>I haven&#39;t tried the left join method. <div class=chatlog__message-group><div id=chatlog__message-container-1271491886401589340 class=chatlog__message-container data-message-id=1271491886401589340><div class=chatlog__message><div class=chatlog__message-aside><img class=chatlog__avatar src=https://cdn.discordapp.com/embed/avatars/4.png alt=Avatar loading=lazy></div><div class=chatlog__message-primary><div class=chatlog__header><span class=chatlog__author title=armslegshandsfeet data-user-id=466248882335252500>armslegshandsfeet</span> <span class=chatlog__timestamp title="Friday, August 9, 2024 12:34 PM"><a href=#chatlog__message-container-1271491886401589340>8/9/2024 12:34 PM</a></span></div><div class="chatlog__content chatlog__markdown"><span class=chatlog__markdown-preserve>Honestly, we cheat a lot. If we&#39;re doing a bunch of WIP, we just <code class="chatlog__markdown-pre chatlog__markdown-pre--inline">--no-verify</code> and move on with it. But we always make sure that &quot;real&quot; commit passes linting. <div class=chatlog__message-group><div id=chatlog__message-container-1272018949315362857 class=chatlog__message-container data-message-id=1272018949315362857><div class=chatlog__message><div class=chatlog__message-aside><img class=chatlog__avatar src="https://cdn.discordapp.com/avatars/114858490555531268/746e25b5e6bc3e73f5a5e166568b153b.png?size=512" alt=Avatar loading=lazy></div><div class=chatlog__message-primary><div class=chatlog__header><span class=chatlog__author title=apatheticlamp data-user-id=114858490555531268>Lamp - Databricks #1 fan</span> <span class=chatlog__timestamp title="Saturday, August 10, 2024 11:29 PM"><a href=#chatlog__message-container-1272018949315362857>8/10/2024 11:29 PM</a></span></div><div class="chatlog__content chatlog__markdown"><span class=chatlog__markdown-preserve>Wondering if this makes sense to people. Say you have users and videos, each video has a 0 to many relationship with &quot;tags&quot;. 
Let&#39;s say you wanted to be able to understand users preferences to certain tags. To do so you build an array or sparse vector of aggregate user watches per tag. 

Then you could calculate that tag &quot;funny&quot; is index 5 so you would do something like
<code class="chatlog__markdown-pre chatlog__markdown-pre--multiline language-sql">WITH user_funny_preference AS (
  SELECT 
    profile_id, 
    SUM(preferences.getItem(5)) / ARRAY_SUM(preferences) AS funny_score
  FROM user_preferences
  GROUP BY profile_id
)</code>
The idea of storing as an array would just be to simplify the table, there would be another table that has the <code class="chatlog__markdown-pre chatlog__markdown-pre--inline">tag_id, tag_name, tag_index</code></span></div></div></div></div></div>

The separation also makes it a bit more robust as depending on the data (work in sports analytics so get all kinds of shit quality) it’s really simple to check that the field is there, let your data scientists work with the data as is (as they will treat it for their modelling as needs be) and then process it through once so that your data analysts etc can work with something more logical</span></div></div></div></div><div id=chatlog__message-container-1272610208413122582 class=chatlog__message-container data-message-id=1272610208413122582><div class=chatlog__message><div class=chatlog__message-aside><div class=chatlog__short-timestamp title="Monday, August 12, 2024 2:38 PM">2:38 PM</div></div><div class=chatlog__message-primary><div class="chatlog__content chatlog__markdown"><span class=chatlog__markdown-preserve>If you validate at the same spot, just have to make sure you don’t “break” stuff if it’s schema validated but values are wrong</span></div></div></div></div><div id=chatlog__message-container-1272610253170540789 class=chatlog__message-container data-message-id=1272610253170540789><div class=chatlog__message><div class=chatlog__message-aside><div class=chatlog__short-timestamp title="Monday, August 12, 2024 2:38 PM">2:38 PM</div></div><div class=chatlog__message-primary><div class="chatlog__content chatlog__markdown"><span class=chatlog__markdown-preserve>Again no right or wrong answers, just have to make it logical</span></div></div></div></div></div>

However unless it&#39;s someone you regularly work with, you don&#39;t know someone else&#39;s knowledge level or what they may or may not correctly assume from the information given. It&#39;s okay to not want to give answers, but if you&#39;re going to give some form of answer, be direct and succinct. No sense in being vague about it. People are here to learn, share information, and much more. So when a learning and teaching opportunity comes up, it&#39;s worth taking the time to either be direct, or say &quot;I can&#39;t/won&#39;t go into detail but here&#39;s a direction to look in.&quot; </span></div></div><div class=chatlog__header><span class=chatlog__author title=wh00h00 data-user-id=689583717064114274>Wh00h00</span> <span class=chatlog__timestamp title="Monday, August 12, 2024 9:41 PM"><a href=#chatlog__message-container-1272716678085611550>8/12/2024 9:41 PM</a></span></div><div class="chatlog__content chatlog__markdown"><span class=chatlog__markdown-preserve>Half of teaching and growing is also to encourage self growth. Learning new skills and abilities, and the ability to google / ChatGPT will serve you way more than getting a direct answer</span></div></div></div></div></div>

Applications for producing and consuming kafka messages, aggregating couple of numbers and putting them in a database for other microservices to use and display. All running in a kubernetes cluster with autoscaling enabled and manually configured numbers of partitions etc. 

From descriptions and examples I can see the tools I mentioned above are doing the exact same thing, but I am not sure what is the actual benefit? I know I am missing something, since these tools are very popular. Do you have any insights to share?</span></div></div></div></div></div>

The <code class="chatlog__markdown-pre chatlog__markdown-pre--inline">thing</code> you mentioned is only <strong>How to make it works</strong>. Let&#39;s ask yourself a few more questions:
<ul><li>Does it work fast and accurately?</li><li>How do you make it work efficiently? (reduce system cost)</li><li>How do others work with it? For e.g: developing, debugging, visualising, etc (reduce human cost)</li><li>How do you monitor and maintain these pipelines?</li><li>How do you deal with pipeline problems? (fault tolerance and disaster recovery)

Those are Engineering aspect. The Data aspect is about business and data quality, rather than how system works under the hood.</li></ul></span> <span class=chatlog__edited-timestamp title="Friday, August 16, 2024 1:28 AM">(edited)</span></div></div></div></div></div>

<div class=chatlog__message-group><div id=chatlog__message-container-1274424808318435400 class=chatlog__message-container data-message-id=1274424808318435400><div class=chatlog__message><div class=chatlog__message-aside><div class=chatlog__reply-symbol></div><img class=chatlog__avatar src="https://cdn.discordapp.com/avatars/527614767674687488/2c224d7c6b2f8913990bcb0f6caee8ec.png?size=512" alt=Avatar loading=lazy></div><div class=chatlog__message-primary><div class=chatlog__reply><img class=chatlog__reply-avatar src="https://cdn.discordapp.com/avatars/341072861617717248/de3c34afcbfc57d434768ee0a08f3d31.png?size=512" alt=Avatar loading=lazy><div class=chatlog__reply-author title=agib1>agi</div><div class=chatlog__reply-content><span class=chatlog__reply-link onclick="scrollToMessage(event,'1274421048217174178')"> having some concerns around because I want to know how they do become one as they are entangled with the whole source of data in their org from what I understand </span></div></div><div class=chatlog__header><span class=chatlog__author title=hadouken_1 data-user-id=527614767674687488>Hadouken!</span> <span class=chatlog__timestamp title="Saturday, August 17, 2024 2:49 PM"><a href=#chatlog__message-container-1274424808318435400>8/17/2024 2:49 PM</a></span></div><div class="chatlog__content chatlog__markdown"><span class=chatlog__markdown-preserve>From chatgpt: 
<div class="chatlog__markdown-quote"><div class="chatlog__markdown-quote-border"></div><div class="chatlog__markdown-quote-content">A Data Architect typically designs and manages the data infrastructure of a company. Their role involves:
</div></div>
<div class="chatlog__markdown-quote"><div class="chatlog__markdown-quote-border"></div><div class="chatlog__markdown-quote-content">1. <strong>Data Modeling</strong>: Creating and maintaining data models that define how data is stored, accessed, and managed across various systems.
2. <strong>Database Design</strong>: Designing databases and data warehouses to ensure data is organized, secure, and accessible.
3. <strong>Integration</strong>: Ensuring that data flows smoothly between systems and is integrated across different platforms.
4. <strong>Governance</strong>: Establishing data standards, policies, and procedures to ensure data quality, security, and compliance.
5. <strong>Collaboration</strong>: Working with other IT professionals, like data engineers and software developers, to implement and optimize data solutions.
</div></div>
<div class="chatlog__markdown-quote"><div class="chatlog__markdown-quote-border"></div><div class="chatlog__markdown-quote-content">In essence, a Data Architect ensures that a company&#39;s data architecture supports its business needs and can scale with growth.</div></div></span></div></div></div></div><div id=chatlog__message-container-1274425002200141958 class=chatlog__message-container data-message-id=1274425002200141958><div class=chatlog__message><div class=chatlog__message-aside><div class=chatlog__short-timestamp title="Saturday, August 17, 2024 2:49 PM">2:49 PM</div></div><div class=chatlog__message-primary><div class="chatlog__content chatlog__markdown"><span class=chatlog__markdown-preserve>I&#39;d say becoming one involves a lot of experience with all those aspects, then convincing a company you know what you&#39;re talking about.</span></div></div></div></div><div id=chatlog__message-container-1274425948321873951 class=chatlog__message-container data-message-id=1274425948321873951><div class=chatlog__message><div class=chatlog__message-aside><div class=chatlog__short-timestamp title="Saturday, August 17, 2024 2:53 PM">2:53 PM</div></div><div class=chatlog__message-primary><div class="chatlog__content chatlog__markdown"><span class=chatlog__markdown-preserve>Similar to a solutions or software architect, but focused on data stuff.</span> <span class=chatlog__edited-timestamp title="Saturday, August 17, 2024 3:00 PM">(edited)</span></div></div></div></div></div>

<div class=chatlog__message-group><div id=chatlog__message-container-1275847496345714801 class=chatlog__message-container data-message-id=1275847496345714801><div class=chatlog__message><div class=chatlog__message-aside><img class=chatlog__avatar src=https://cdn.discordapp.com/embed/avatars/3.png alt=Avatar loading=lazy></div><div class=chatlog__message-primary><div class=chatlog__header><span class=chatlog__author title=paulrpg data-user-id=339851938118238219>paulrpg</span> <span class=chatlog__timestamp title="Wednesday, August 21, 2024 1:02 PM"><a href=#chatlog__message-container-1275847496345714801>8/21/2024 1:02 PM</a></span></div><div class="chatlog__content chatlog__markdown"><span class=chatlog__markdown-preserve>Has anything been written about design patterns in dbt? An example is particular types of aggregations we need to do.

An example is that we get status updates for a thing where each status update is its own unique object. If we want to rollup to look at the lifecycle of the thing we can build an incremental model, take the new rows of status updates, bring in the other status updates for our thing and recalculate our aggregation. This seems to be quite performant when compared to other things I&#39;ve tried but willing to take criticism for it.

I guess what I&#39;m looking for is just more data modelling literature</span></div></div></div></div></div>

<div class=chatlog__message-group><div id=chatlog__message-container-1276027484688744488 class=chatlog__message-container data-message-id=1276027484688744488><div class=chatlog__message><div class=chatlog__message-aside><img class=chatlog__avatar src="https://cdn.discordapp.com/avatars/114858490555531268/746e25b5e6bc3e73f5a5e166568b153b.png?size=512" alt=Avatar loading=lazy></div><div class=chatlog__message-primary><div class=chatlog__header><span class=chatlog__author title=apatheticlamp data-user-id=114858490555531268>Lamp - Databricks #1 fan</span> <span class=chatlog__timestamp title="Thursday, August 22, 2024 12:57 AM"><a href=#chatlog__message-container-1276027484688744488>8/22/2024 12:57 AM</a></span></div><div class="chatlog__content chatlog__markdown"><span class=chatlog__markdown-preserve>What are peoples thoughts here about building out SDKs for your tables
Example
<code class="chatlog__markdown-pre chatlog__markdown-pre--multiline language-python">class UserProfileTable:
  PROFILE_ID: str = &#39;profile_id&#39;
  LOCATION: str = &#39;location&#39;
  LAST_LOGIN: str = &#39;last_login_utc&#39;
  CREATION_DATE: str = &#39;created_at_utc&#39;

  def __init__(self, env: str):
    self.catalog = &#39;hive_metastore&#39;
    self.schema = &#39;core_data_prod&#39; if env = &#39;prod&#39; else &#39;core_data_dev&#39;
    self.table = &#39;user_profile&#39;

  @property
  def full_table_name(self):
    return f&#39;{self.catalog}.{self.schema}.{self.table}&#39;

  def get_dateframe(self) -&gt; pyspark.sql.DataFrame:
    return spark.table(self.full_table_name)

  def get_active_users(self) -&gt; pyspark.sql.DataFrame:
    return self.get_dataframe().filter(F.col(UserProfileTable.LAST_LOGIN) &gt;= &#39;2024-08-01&#39;)</code></span></div></div></div></div><div id=chatlog__message-container-1276028753381953609 class=chatlog__message-container data-message-id=1276028753381953609><div class=chatlog__message><div class=chatlog__message-aside><div class=chatlog__short-timestamp title="Thursday, August 22, 2024 1:02 AM">1:02 AM</div></div><div class=chatlog__message-primary><div class="chatlog__content chatlog__markdown"><span class=chatlog__markdown-preserve>The benefit I&#39;m thinking about here is you could version out your tables with the SDK
The SDK would also contain scripts that actually produce the tables as well
Then users don&#39;t have to worry as much about what specific column names are, or logic to get the latest data, etc.</span></div></div></div></div></div>

<code class="chatlog__markdown-pre chatlog__markdown-pre--multiline language-python">class UserProfileTable:
  PROFILE_ID: str = &#39;profile_id&#39;
  LOCATION: str = &#39;location&#39;
  LAST_LOGIN: str = &#39;last_login_utc&#39;
  CREATION_DATE: str = &#39;created_at_utc&#39;

  def __init__(self, env: str):
    self.catalog = &#39;hive_metastore&#39;
    self.schema = &#39;core_data_prod&#39; if env = &#39;prod&#39; else &#39;core_data_dev&#39;
    self.table = &#39;user_profile&#39;

  @property
  def full_table_name(self):
    return f&#39;{self.catalog}.{self.schema}.{self.table}&#39;

  def get_dateframe(self) -&gt; pyspark.sql.DataFrame:
    return spark.table(self.full_table_name)

  def get_active_users(self) -&gt; pyspark.sql.DataFrame:
    return self.get_dataframe().filter(F.col(UserProfileTable.LAST_LOGIN) &gt;= &#39;2024-08-01&#39;)</code> </span></div></div><div class=chatlog__header><span class=chatlog__author title=paulrpg data-user-id=339851938118238219>paulrpg</span> <span class=chatlog__timestamp title="Thursday, August 22, 2024 2:13 PM"><a href=#chatlog__message-container-1276227850386673667>8/22/2024 2:13 PM</a></span></div><div class="chatlog__content chatlog__markdown"><span class=chatlog__markdown-preserve>reminds me a lot of spring boot where you can define tables by building a java class. You could automate the creation of this. I can see the benefit of wrapping sql statements in functions/methods to encapsulate the logic but if you want to version your sdk you now need to also support multiple versions of it.

I&#39;ve had versions assigned to tables but it has been used to manage migrations of systems. If we have a newer version of the code it can sit and run migration scripts to update the table. The actual SDK is just for the current version of the code</span></div></div></div></div><div id=chatlog__message-container-1276228072298905751 class=chatlog__message-container data-message-id=1276228072298905751><div class=chatlog__message><div class=chatlog__message-aside><div class=chatlog__short-timestamp title="Thursday, August 22, 2024 2:14 PM">2:14 PM</div></div><div class=chatlog__message-primary><div class="chatlog__content chatlog__markdown"><span class=chatlog__markdown-preserve>To me, the point in designing data intensive applications rings true, why use a general purpose language to solve a data access issue when  sql is designed as a query language</span></div></div></div></div></div>

I know it varies based on the workflow, people, etc. But just curious if anyone has found any solution that they think is a good balance that is both not a headache and also useful for different kinds of people to use. Feel like there&#39;s the pitfalls of using file-explorer, using a software that can be fidgety to use for a portion of the team/creates barriers to utility and eventually falls out of favor to just &quot;be there&quot;, and then some less supported ways that could break later on (like some sort of app). <div class=chatlog__message-group><div id=chatlog__message-container-1277535642380795925 class=chatlog__message-container data-message-id=1277535642380795925><div class=chatlog__message><div class=chatlog__message-aside><img class=chatlog__avatar src="https://cdn.discordapp.com/avatars/984386111709253672/23fac11e09942718016d6d4c58935a2e.png?size=512" alt=Avatar loading=lazy></div><div class=chatlog__message-primary><div class=chatlog__header><span class=chatlog__author title=rebirch data-user-id=984386111709253672>reBirch</span> <span class=chatlog__timestamp title="Monday, August 26, 2024 4:50 AM"><a href=#chatlog__message-container-1277535642380795925>8/26/2024 4:50 AM</a></span></div><div class="chatlog__content chatlog__markdown"><span class=chatlog__markdown-preserve><a href="https://world.hey.com/dhh/how-to-recover-from-microservices-ce3803cc">https://world.hey.com/dhh/how-to-recover-from-microservices-ce3803cc</a>
I&#39;m kind of late to the party with this, but I do wonder why DHH hates microservices so much.</span></div><div class=chatlog__embed><div class="chatlog__embed-color-pill chatlog__embed-color-pill--default"></div><div class=chatlog__embed-content-container><div class=chatlog__embed-content><div class=chatlog__embed-text><div class=chatlog__embed-title><a class=chatlog__embed-title-link href=https://world.hey.com/dhh/how-to-recover-from-microservices-ce3803cc><div class="chatlog__markdown chatlog__markdown-preserve">How to recover from microservices</div></a></div><div class=chatlog__embed-description><div class="chatlog__markdown chatlog__markdown-preserve">I won&#39;t deny there may well be cases where a microservices-first architecture makes sense, but I think they&#39;re few and far in between. The vast majority of systems are much better served by starting and staying with a majestic monolith. The Prime Video case study that blew up the internet yesterday is but the latest illustration. Maybe...</div></div></div><div class=chatlog__embed-thumbnail-container><a class=chatlog__embed-thumbnail-link href=https://images-ext-1.discordapp.net/external/DKvav-ZYXz7zKau661mC8sSguplRQIQIPVusJrY1WVE/https/world.hey.com/dhh/avatar-fb368b1ee9b185dc2a09b03eabdb61678dd55244> <img class=chatlog__embed-thumbnail src=https://images-ext-1.discordapp.net/external/DKvav-ZYXz7zKau661mC8sSguplRQIQIPVusJrY1WVE/https/world.hey.com/dhh/avatar-fb368b1ee9b185dc2a09b03eabdb61678dd55244 alt=Thumbnail loading=lazy> </a></div></div></div></div></div></div></div><div id=chatlog__message-container-1277536503060238406 class=chatlog__message-container data-message-id=1277536503060238406><div class=chatlog__message><div class=chatlog__message-aside><div class=chatlog__short-timestamp title="Monday, August 26, 2024 4:53 AM">4:53 AM</div></div><div class=chatlog__message-primary><div class="chatlog__content chatlog__markdown"><span class=chatlog__markdown-preserve>I mean, microservices to architecture is what aggressive separation-of-concern factoring is to a single application&#39;s code base. Yes, it&#39;s easier to build a single huge thing first and then, once it&#39;s stable and you understand where the logical breaks really are, refactor it. And yes, you can make mistakes when refactoring it because you chose the wrong abstraction/wrong pattern/etc. But that doesn&#39;t mean that separation of concern is a useless principle.</span></div></div></div></div></div>
<div class=chatlog__message-group><div id=chatlog__message-container-1277546059077255189 class=chatlog__message-container data-message-id=1277546059077255189><div class=chatlog__message><div class=chatlog__message-primary><div class=chatlog__header><span class=chatlog__author style=color:rgb(46,204,113) title=kahnwong data-user-id=161154369763409921>kahnwong</span> <span class=chatlog__timestamp title="Monday, August 26, 2024 5:31 AM"><a href=#chatlog__message-container-1277546059077255189>8/26/2024 5:31 AM</a></span></div><div class="chatlog__content chatlog__markdown"><span class=chatlog__markdown-preserve>microservices is not useless, but often people use it the wrong way</span></div></div></div></div><div id=chatlog__message-container-1277546243790340189 class=chatlog__message-container data-message-id=1277546243790340189><div class=chatlog__message><div class=chatlog__message-aside><div class=chatlog__short-timestamp title="Monday, August 26, 2024 5:32 AM">5:32 AM</div></div><div class=chatlog__message-primary><div class="chatlog__content chatlog__markdown"><span class=chatlog__markdown-preserve>you should start out with a monolith, yes. but you don&#39;t have to refactor every part into a microservices if you don&#39;t need to</span></div></div></div></div><div id=chatlog__message-container-1277546581599453241 class=chatlog__message-container data-message-id=1277546581599453241><div class=chatlog__message><div class=chatlog__message-aside><div class=chatlog__short-timestamp title="Monday, August 26, 2024 5:34 AM">5:34 AM</div></div><div class=chatlog__message-primary><div class="chatlog__content chatlog__markdown"><span class=chatlog__markdown-preserve>usually a good sign when you should split into a microservice is when certain routes get triggered more often, and is the cause of your autoscaling triggers</span></div></div></div></div><div id=chatlog__message-container-1277546799086702623 class=chatlog__message-container data-message-id=1277546799086702623><div class=chatlog__message><div class=chatlog__message-aside><div class=chatlog__short-timestamp title="Monday, August 26, 2024 5:34 AM">5:34 AM</div></div><div class=chatlog__message-primary><div class="chatlog__content chatlog__markdown"><span class=chatlog__markdown-preserve>microservices is more of a organizational modeling problem. not many people can get it right</span></div></div></div></div><div id=chatlog__message-container-1277546910588342293 class=chatlog__message-container data-message-id=1277546910588342293><div class=chatlog__message><div class=chatlog__message-aside><div class=chatlog__short-timestamp title="Monday, August 26, 2024 5:35 AM">5:35 AM</div></div><div class=chatlog__message-primary><div class="chatlog__content chatlog__markdown"><span class=chatlog__markdown-preserve>but you are free to experiment with your version of microservices model. some approaches might work for you. iterate, rinse and repeat</span></div></div></div></div></div>

<div class=chatlog__message-group><div id=chatlog__message-container-1277633488421523549 class=chatlog__message-container data-message-id=1277633488421523549><div class=chatlog__message><div class=chatlog__message-aside><img class=chatlog__avatar src="https://cdn.discordapp.com/avatars/120645994923687937/a0b1bdb86d7551eb9267efe6cc7b5f40.png?size=512" alt=Avatar loading=lazy></div><div class=chatlog__message-primary><div class=chatlog__header><span class=chatlog__author title=rexeh data-user-id=120645994923687937>Rexeh</span> <span class=chatlog__timestamp title="Monday, August 26, 2024 11:19 AM"><a href=#chatlog__message-container-1277633488421523549>8/26/2024 11:19 AM</a></span></div><div class="chatlog__content chatlog__markdown"><span class=chatlog__markdown-preserve>I had my first ooof on weekend. We pushed a new pipeline live Thursday and I monitored it Friday, luckily not being used in production just to monitor / gather latency stats.

Saw weird batch times of ~15 mins, took 13 hours to populate table but thought hey is a fair bit of data to take from silver. Once live noticed a join was always coming back null, turns out we had a bad requirement where this join key would never exist in target table.

Roll onto Friday evening after a few drinks I decide to just look at the DAG, and it dawned on me. This thing is taking 15 min a batch because it&#39;s reading 1TB full scans every 15 mins, on a continuous process across 4 geos. Did some napkin math and worked out it could be 4 figures cost over bank holiday weekend <img
